        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1201256982">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1201256982" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20446197-cindy-dyson-eitelman" class="left imgcol" title="Cindy Dyson Eitelman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369063290p2/20446197.jpg" alt="Cindy Dyson Eitelman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1201256982?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20446197-cindy-dyson-eitelman" class="user" title="Cindy Dyson Eitelman">Cindy Dyson Eitelman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/95907.Bad_Badder_Baddest" title="Paperback 9780330398220" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1201256982">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3069629099470154578">Cynthia Voigt's <em>Bad, Badder, Baddest</em> had cover hype telling the biggest lie I've ever read. (In a cover blurb.) One of the bad girls wasn't bad at all, one suffered from poor impulse control and the normal human desire for excitement, and the third was so tangential to the story she never even got to be a "point of view" character. <br /><br />So, no--the girls weren't bad. But the book wasn't bad either--IMHO Cynthia Voigt is incapable of writing a bad book.<br /><br />I'd have enjoyed it more as a teenager.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8289409118198324425">Didn't like it. Which is unfortunate. It was definitely written for younger kids, but usually that doesn't bother me.<br /><br />The entire book is about Mikey and Margalo, who are trying to stop one of their parents from getting divorced. Literally, the whole book. 80% of it is them discussing it, trying to figure out what to do.             Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37871242">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11991245299637452888">I cannot tell if I would have enjoyed this story more had I read it at 10 or 11. I had a hard time distinguishing between Mikey and Margalo for the first several pages, and I think I had the same problem years ago with Bad Girls. The girls are outwardly intent on keeping up their "bad" image and argue and act tough a lot. I found their attitudes and interactions at times forced. Other times, however, they had delightful and surprising exchanges. There's not much of a plot here, but I am determin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11991245299637452888">I cannot tell if I would have enjoyed this story more had I read it at 10 or 11. I had a hard time distinguishing between Mikey and Margalo for the first several pages, and I think I had the same problem years ago with Bad Girls. The girls are outwardly intent on keeping up their "bad" image and argue and act tough a lot. I found their attitudes and interactions at times forced. Other times, however, they had delightful and surprising exchanges. There's not much of a plot here, but I am determined to finish the series, as I am a loyal Voigt fan.<br /><br />33/60 tbr box.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Nrcm0mbC6puAW4bDKaqyvF5tLvRMrHXV0z0SluyiAWRTYxkBlBD+YQyD8nhXy1QOF5rt7QVxMn+5NBcEIDf3IQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IoB7rlibGGRwULfHTGiQrcdL7iDIN0ggrBpkXsIWyqhHVER9qkkMnvyIw3wyCXYfjrwtOYHqD4rGE2HMDoM87Q==')})
  }

Zarrow Award, for lifetime achievement, 2003<br />The Margaret Edwards Award, for a body of work, 1995<br /><em>Jackaroo</em>: Ratte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17349659310760388391">Cynthia Voigt is an American author of books for young adults dealing with various topics such as adventure, mystery, racism and child abuse. <br /><br /><br /><strong>Awards:</strong> <br /><em>Angus and Sadie</em>: the Sequoyah Book Award (given by readers in Oklahoma), 2008<br />The Katahdin Award, for lifetime achievement, 2003<br />The Anne V. Big trouble...Mikey Elsinger isn\'t the romantic type. She thinks that most boys are just brainless meatheads. Girls who like brainless meatheads are too weird for words. Margalo Epps likes to admire boys from afar. Maybe a movie star, or even (don\'t tell anyone!) a teacher. But most of the boys at school stink (some of them literally). Enter Shawn Macavity. Technically, he\'s a brainless meathead. But he\'s gorgeous. Really, really gorgeous. Thwack. Cupid\'s arrow strikes its target. The world has changed for ever. Mikey is in LURRRVE. And Margalo is NOT impressed...The fourth funny, touching book about bad girls Mikey and Margalo&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"16037129269603816145\" href=\"#\"
